Look at the net/sunrpc/xprtrdma/rpc_rdma.c code at lines 104-108:```c\nif (!ppages[p]) {    /* alloc the pagelist for receiving buffer */\n    ppages[p] = alloc_page(GFP_ATOMIC);    if (!ppages[p])\n        return -ENOMEM;}\n```\n\nThis is using GFP_ATOMIC to allocate pages for the RPC receive buffer. RPC layer tries to copy the reply into the receive buffer4. If pages need to be allocated (GFP_ATOMIC), the allocation might fail if memory is low5. Advance ppage by the number of pages in that offset\n3. Mask base to get just the offset within the final page\n4. That's why the current code is wrong—it's reducing pglen by the wrong base We're subtracting the ORIGINAL base value from pglen, but we should be subtracting the ADJUSTED base value (after adding page_base and masking to get the offset).\n\nHere's the correct sequence:\n1. Add page_base to base to get absolute position in the page array\n2. Use that to calculate which page we start at and what offset within that page\n3. THEN subtract that offset from pglen\n\nCurrently it's doing:\n1. Subtract original base from pglen\n2. Then adjust base\n\nSo pglen gets the wrong value subtracted!\n\nThis causes pglen (the remaining page length to copy) to be incorrectly calculated, which leads to attempting to copy more or fewer bytes than available, causing buffer underrun or corruption, which then fails XDR decoding, which manifests as \"getattr failed\" error.\n\nThis is exactly the kind of subtle bug that would cause intermittent failures depending on the page layout and amount of data being copied. During autofs mount expiration, when inode revalidation happens, if the reply buffer has a specific page layout that triggers this bug, the incomplete or corrupted buffer causes the getattr to fail.\n\nThe fix is to move the pglen -= base line to AFTER the base adjustment, so it subtracts the correct (adjusted) base value:\n\n\n```c\nif (base || xdr->page_base) {\n    base += xdr->page_base;\n    ppage += base >> PAGE_CACHE_SHIFT;\n    base &= ~PAGE_CACHE_MASK;\n    pglen -= base;  <-- MOVE THIS LINE HERE\n}\n```\n\nAlternatively, I could change line 97 to directly subtract the masked offset without reordering: `pglen -= (base + xdr->page_base) & PAGE_CACHE_MASK;`. Here's a summary of my findings:\n\n## Fault Localization Summary\n\n**Buggy File:** `net/sunrpc/socklib.c`  \n**Buggy Function:** `xdr_partial_copy_from_skb()`  \n**Confidence Level:** 0.95\n\n### The Bug\n\nIn the `xdr_partial_copy_from_skb()` function at lines 96-101, there is an **order-of-operations bug** that causes incorrect calculation of the page length (`pglen`) when copying data from socket buffers to XDR buffers.\n\n**Problematic Code:**\n```c\nif (base || xdr->page_base) {\n    pglen -= base;        // LINE 97: Subtracts ORIGINAL base value\n    base += xdr->page_base;  // LINE 98: Adjusts base\n    ppage += base >> PAGE_CACHE_SHIFT;  // LINE 99: Advances page pointer\n    base &= ~PAGE_CACHE_MASK;  // LINE 100: Masks to get offset within page\n}\n```\n\n### The Issue\n\nLine 97 subtracts the **original `base` value** from `pglen` before `base` is adjusted by adding `xdr->page_base` and masking. This causes `pglen` to have an **incorrect value** that doesn't match the actual offset within the first page of data.\n\nThe correct sequence should be:\n1. Adjust `base` to the absolute offset (add `page_base`)\n2. Calculate which page we start at\n3. This causes `pglen` to have an **incorrect value** that doesn't match the actual offset within the first page of data.\n\nThe correct sequence should be:\n1. Mask `base` to get the offset **within** that page\n4. **THEN** subtract this adjusted `base` from `pglen`\n\n### Impact on the Bug Report\n\nThis order-of-operations bug causes:\n- RPC reply buffers to be copied incompletely or incorrectly\n- XDR decoding to fail when parsing the reply\n- NFS `nfs_revalidate_inode()` to report \"getattr failed\" error (-512)\n- During autofs mount expiration, this causes the /storage mount to disappear along with the mounted volumes\n- The tcpdump shows the server replies successfully, but the client treats it as an error due to the corrupted/incomplete buffer\n\nThe result file has been written to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`.","stop_reason":null,"session_id":"0e080e13-bd8d-4065-8b2e-ca1a15ec718c","total_cost_usd":0.34600445,"usage":{"input_tokens":215,"cache_creation_input_tokens":93255,"cache_read_input_tokens":1642607,"output_tokens":12992,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":93255,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"},"modelUsage":{"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001":{"inputTokens":215,"outputTokens":12992,"cacheReadInputTokens":1642607,"cacheCreationInputTokens":93255,"webSearchRequests":0,"costUSD":0.34600445,"contextWindow":200000,"maxOutputTokens":32000}},"permission_denials":[],"fast_mode_state":"off","uuid":"d834bcfb-8930-4d0f-a9d6-0281e652fe7f"}
